Round-robin iteration through queues (line 786)\n2. For each non-empty queue, compute the virtual finish time of its oldest request:\n   - `virtualFinish = queue.nextDispatchR + request.totalWork()`\n   - `queue.nextDispatchR` is the \"virtual start time\" for the next request in this queue\n   - `request.totalWork()` is the work (seat-seconds) for this request\n\n3. Select the queue with minimum virtual finish time (line 797)\n4. Tie-breaking: First queue in round-robin order wins (implicit in loop order)\n\n**Dispatch**:\n1. Dequeue the oldest request from the selected queue (line 822)\n2. Set `request.decision` to `decisionExecute` via its promise (line 710)\n3. Move the request from `requestsWaiting` to `requestsExecuting` (line 722)\n4. Update the queue's `nextDispatchR` by adding the request's total work (line 741)\n5. Apply anti-windup hack (line 952): Ensure `nextDispatchR >= oldestWaiting.arrivalR` to prevent virtual time from exceeding arrival time\n\n#### Phase 5: Request Execution and Completion (Finish)\n\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:381\u2013395`\n\n```go\nfunc (req *request) Finish(execFn func()) bool {\n    exec, idle := req.wait()\n    if !exec {\n        return idle\n    }\n    defer func() {\n        idle = req.qs.finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible(req)\n    }()\n    execFn()\n    return idle\n}\n```\n\n**Steps**:\n1. Call `req.wait()` to obtain the dispatch decision (line 382)\n   - Blocks on `decision.Get()` until a decision is available\n   - If context is cancelled, decision is automatically set to `decisionCancel`\n   - If decision is `decisionCancel`, return false (request is rejected)\n\n2. If decision is `decisionExecute`, execute the callback (line 391)\n\n3. Call `finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible()` (line 388):\n   - Acquire lock, sync time (line 852)\n   - Call `finishRequestLocked(req)` (line 855)\n     - Decrement `totRequestsExecuting` (line 865)\n     - Calculate actual service duration (line 869)\n     - Update queue's `nextDispatchR` by subtracting the delta between estimated and actual service time (line 938)\n     - Apply anti-windup again (line 939)\n     - Release seats (line 877) or schedule delayed release for additional latency phase (line 915-929)\n     - Remove queue if it's become empty and we have excess queues (line 966-984)\n   - Call `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()` again (line 856)\n   - Return idle status\n\n### 3.3 Virtual Time Mechanics\n\n#### Virtual Time Synchronization (syncTimeLocked)\n\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:461\u2013479`\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) syncTimeLocked(ctx context.Context) {\n    realNow := qs.clock.Now()\n    timeSinceLast := realNow.Sub(qs.lastRealTime)\n    qs.lastRealTime = realNow\n    prevR := qs.currentR\n    incrR := fqrequest.SeatsTimesDuration(qs.getVirtualTimeRatioLocked(), timeSinceLast)\n    qs.currentR = prevR + incrR\n    ...\n}\n```\n\n**Key insight**: Virtual time advances proportionally to the \"virtual time ratio\":\n\n```\nvirtual time ratio = min(total seat requests, ConcurrencyLimit) / number of active queues\n```\n\nThis ensures that:\n- If 10 queues are active and concurrency limit is 100 seats, each queue gets 10 seat-seconds per real second\n- If only 1 queue is active, it gets the full 100 seat-seconds per real second\n- If queues request 200 seats but concurrency limit is 100, queues advance at 100 seat-seconds per real second\n\n#### Virtual Time Overflow Mitigation (Epoch Advancement)\n\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:481\u2013522`\n\n```go\nconst rDecrement = fqrequest.MaxSeatSeconds / 2\nconst highR = rDecrement + rDecrement/2\n\nfunc (qs *queueSet) advanceEpoch(ctx context.Context, now time.Time, incrR fqrequest.SeatSeconds) {\n    oldR := qs.currentR\n    qs.currentR -= rDecrement\n    // Decrement all queue.nextDispatchR and request.arrivalR by rDecrement\n    ...\n}\n```\n\n**Why it's needed**:\n- `SeatSeconds` is a float64, which can overflow after very long running (e.g., years of operation)\n- When `currentR` exceeds `highR` (MaxSeatSeconds \u00d7 0.75), the system \"advances the epoch\" by subtracting `MaxSeatSeconds \u00d7 0.5` from all progress meters\n- This is equivalent to resetting the coordinate system while preserving relative ordering\n\n---\n\n## 4. Fairness Guarantees and Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Fairness Model\n\nThe QueueSet provides **work-conserving fair queuing** with the following properties:\n\n1. **Weighted Fairness**: Each queue receives service proportional to its share of active demand\n   - Fair share = `ConcurrencyLimit / num_active_queues`\n   - A queue with more requests waiting gets no preferential treatment; it's enqueued in the same queues as low-demand flows\n\n2. **Virtual Time Ordering**: Dispatch is strictly ordered by virtual finish time\n   - If two queues are both active and have the same concurrency limit share, the queue with the smaller virtual finish time is served first\n   - This prevents a queue from \"jumping ahead\" by having broader requests\n\n3. **Shuffle Sharding Balancing**: Requests within the same flow are scattered across multiple queues\n   - A single bursty flow occupies only `handSize` queues instead of monopolizing one\n   - This reduces head-of-line blocking (slow requests don't block the entire flow)\n\n### 4.2 Known Limitations and Tradeoffs\n\n#### 4.2.1 Single Global Lock\n\n**Tradeoff**: All mutable state is protected by a single `sync.Mutex`.\n\n**Impact**:\n- Ensures correctness and consistency (no race conditions between queue selection and dispatch)\n- Can become a bottleneck if `StartRequest()`, `Finish()`, and dispatch loops contend heavily\n- Latency of virtual time updates is bounded by lock-holding time\n\n**Mitigation**: Lock-holding periods are kept small; expensive operations (like metrics recording) happen outside the lock.\n\n#### 4.2.2 Shuffle Sharding Overhead\n\n**Tradeoff**: Shuffle sharding requires `Dealer.Deal()` to generate a hand of queue indices via modular arithmetic.\n\n**Cost**: O(handSize) bit operations per enqueue (negligible; typically handSize \u2264 15).\n\n**Benefit**: Prevents a single bursty flow from monopolizing one queue.\n\n#### 4.2.3 Virtual Time Estimation Errors\n\n**Tradeoff**: Service time is estimated via `estimatedServiceDuration` (default 3ms); actual times may vary.\n\n**Impact**:\n- If actual service time < estimate, queue's `nextDispatchR` is incremented (punishing the queue for being faster)\n- If actual service time > estimate, queue's `nextDispatchR` is decremented (rewarding the queue for being slower)\n- This dampens oscillations but introduces bias if estimates are consistently wrong\n\n**Mitigation**: The estimate is conservative (3ms is a typical list operation); most requests are faster, so queues are rarely punished. Configurable via code, not via API objects.\n\n#### 4.2.4 Queue Removal by Attrition\n\n**Tradeoff**: Reducing `DesiredNumQueues` doesn't immediately remove excess queues; they drain by attrition (when they become empty).\n\n**Impact**:\n- If a queue has long-lived requests, the queue persists even after desired count drops\n- During configuration updates, total queue count may temporarily exceed desired count\n\n**Benefit**: Avoids disrupting in-flight requests; maintains isolation guarantees.\n\n#### 4.2.5 Seat-Based Work Model Limitations\n\n**Tradeoff**: Work is modeled as \"seats \u00d7 duration\"; actual CPU, memory, and I/O costs are not distinguished.\n\n**Impact**:\n- A 100-seat request that does I/O-only work monopolizes concurrency but uses little CPU\n- A 1-seat request with heavy CPU computation is starved\n- Seat allocation is per-priority-level, so no cross-priority admission decisions are made here\n\n**Mitigation**: Work estimation is delegable (via `workEstimator` parameter); custom estimators can cap seats per request type (e.g., watch operations vs. list operations).\n\n#### 4.2.6 No Preemption\n\n**Tradeoff**: Once a request is executing, it cannot be preempted; dispatch is only at the boundary (when a request calls `Finish()`).\n\n**Impact**:\n- A low-priority request that is currently executing blocks dispatch of high-priority requests\n- Wait times are bounded by the longest executing request\n\n**Rationale**: Preemption in HTTP request processing is complex (state cleanup, partial response handling); not feasible for a general-purpose API server.\n\n### 4.3 Fairness in Practice\n\n**Example scenario**: Two flows A and B, each with a queue, and ConcurrencyLimit = 10 seats.\n\n1. Flow A sends 5 requests, each requiring 4 seats (total 20 seats demanded)\n2. Flow B sends 1 request requiring 2 seats\n3. Initial dispatch:\n   - Both flows are active, so virtual time ratio = min(20+2, 10) / 2 = 5 seat-seconds per real second per queue\n   - If all 5 of A's requests start, they occupy 20 seats > 10 limit, so only 2.5 on average can run\n   - Request 1 of A gets dispatched, occupies 4 seats (6 remain)\n   - Request 1 of B gets dispatched, occupies 2 seats (4 remain)\n   - Request 2 of A gets dispatched, occupies 4 seats (0 remain)\n   - Dispatch loop exits: no more seats\n\n4. Virtual time advances as requests execute:\n   - If A's request 1 takes 1 second at 4 seats, its virtual finish time = arrivalR + 4 * 1 = arrivalR + 4\n   - If B's request takes 1 second at 2 seats, its virtual finish time = arrivalR + 2 * 1 = arrivalR + 2\n   - B's request finishes first (lower virtual finish time)\n   - When B's request completes, B has released 2 seats; A's queue 3 can now be dispatched\n\n---\n\n## 5. Failure Modes and Design Limits\n\n### 5.1 Virtual Time Overflow\n\n**Condition**: `currentR` exceeds `MaxSeatSeconds` (float64 ~= 9.22e18 seat-seconds)\n\n**Effect**: Epoch advancement is triggered, subtracting `rDecrement` from all progress meters\n\n**Manifestation**: Logs show \"Advancing epoch\" message (line 495)\n\n**Limits**: With ConcurrencyLimit = 5000 and continuous load, overflow occurs after ~60 million years (not a practical concern)\n\n### 5.2 Queue Underflow\n\n**Condition**: During epoch advancement, `queue.nextDispatchR` or `request.arrivalR` would underflow (become larger after subtraction)\n\n**Effect**: Logged as error: \"Underflow\" (line 507-508)\n\n**Causes**: Rare; indicates a logic error in virtual time management (e.g., nextDispatchR not properly advanced after dispatch)\n\n### 5.3 Request Dispatch Before Arrival\n\n**Condition**: `queue.nextDispatchR < request.arrivalR` after dequeue\n\n**Effect**: Logged as error: \"dispatch before arrival\" (line 840)\n\n**Rationale**: This is prevented by the anti-windup hack (boundNextDispatchLocked), which ensures nextDispatchR >= arrivalR\n\n### 5.4 Concurrency Limit Exceeded\n\n**Condition**: `totSeatsInUse + request.MaxSeats() > ConcurrencyLimit` when a request is dispatched\n\n**Detection**: During dispatch, `canAccommodateSeatsLocked()` is checked; should prevent dispatch if violated\n\n**Fallback**: Requests with `MaxSeats > ConcurrencyLimit` can only proceed when all other requests are idle (line 757-760)\n\n### 5.5 Promise Decision Not Set\n\n**Condition**: A request's decision is never set (neither execute nor cancel)\n\n**Detection**: `req.wait()` blocks indefinitely on `decision.Get()`; context timeout sets decision to cancel\n\n**Causes**: Logic error in dispatch loop (should not happen if dispatchLocked() properly calls `decision.Set()`)\n\n### 5.6 Queue Length Limit Exceeded\n\n**Condition**: More requests are enqueued than `QueueLengthLimit * DesiredNumQueues`\n\n**Detection**: Checked in `rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked()` (line 623)\n\n**Fallback**: Request is rejected with \"queue-full\" reason\n\n---\n\n## 6. Configuration and Reconfiguration\n\n### 6.1 Two-Phase Creation\n\nThe factory pattern enables validation before committing resources:\n\n```go\n// Phase 1: Validate queuing config (expensive only if invalid)\ncompleter, err := factory.BeginConstruction(queuingConfig)\nif err != nil {\n    return err  // Reject before allocating queues\n}\n\n// Phase 2: Allocate dispatching capacity\nqs := completer.Complete(dispatchingConfig)\n```\n\n**Benefit**: Errors in one part of config (e.g., invalid HandSize) are caught before the other part is committed.\n\n### 6.2 Reconfiguration via Configuration Change\n\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:239\u2013287`\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) BeginConfigChange(qCfg fq.QueuingConfig) (fq.QueueSetCompleter, error)\nfunc (qs *queueSet) setConfiguration(ctx context.Context, qCfg fq.QueuingConfig,\n    dealer *shufflesharding.Dealer, dCfg fq.DispatchingConfig)\n```\n\n**Behavior**:\n- If `DesiredNumQueues` increases, new queues are immediately created (line 264-265)\n- If `DesiredNumQueues` decreases (or becomes zero), queues are removed by attrition (no immediate removal)\n- If `DesiredNumQueues` becomes zero, queuing is disabled; concurrency limit is the only constraint\n- If `DesiredNumQueues` becomes negative, the queue set is \"exempt\" from all limits (used for system-critical requests)\n\n**Metrics update**: `reqsGaugePair.RequestsWaiting.SetDenominator()` and related calls (line 282-284) adjust prometheus denominator for ratio gauges.\n\n### 6.3 Stable Reconfigurations\n\n**Invariant**: Configurations that don't change `DesiredNumQueues` do not alter the queue structure.\n\nExample: Increasing `ConcurrencyLimit` only updates `dCfg.ConcurrencyDenominator` and may trigger borrowing at the controller level; no queue reorganization.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 7.1 Clock Abstraction\n\n**Interface**: `eventclock.Interface` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/eventclock/interface.go)\n\n**Extensibility**:\n- Real implementations: `eventclock.Real{}` for production\n- Fake implementations: Synthetic time progression for testing\n- Custom implementations: Could support timescale acceleration, pausing, etc.\n\n**Risk**: Incorrect time progression breaks virtual time invariants (e.g., currentR should be monotonically increasing).\n\n### 7.2 Promise Factory\n\n**Interface**: `promise.WriteOnce` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/promise/promise.go)\n\n**Extensibility**:\n- Default: Uses channels and `sync.Once`\n- Test factories: Can inject counting or blocking behavior\n- Custom: Could implement alternative synchronization (e.g., callback-based instead of blocking)\n\n**Risk**: Non-blocking or multi-set implementations would violate the \"write-once\" contract.\n\n### 7.3 Work Estimator\n\n**Interface**: `WorkEstimatorFunc` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/width.go:89)\n\n**Current implementations**:\n- `ListWorkEstimator`: Estimates seats for list operations based on object count\n- `MutatingWorkEstimator`: Estimates seats for mutations based on watcher count and object count\n\n**Extensibility**:\n- Custom estimators can override or extend for domain-specific request types\n- Can cap seats per-request, per-priority-level (via `MaxSeatsTracker`)\n- Injected at controller level; affects all queues under that controller\n\n**Risk**: Wildly inaccurate estimates (e.g., 100% overestimation) can cause severe underutilization; conversely, underestimation can overload the server.\n\n### 7.4 Flow Distinguisher\n\n**Purpose**: Hash input for shuffle sharding; ensures requests from the same flow are scattered\n\n**Customization**: Determined by `FlowSchema.Spec.DistinguisherMethod` in the config API\n- `None`: All requests to this priority level are treated as one flow; one queue or distributed equally\n- `ByUser`: Requests are grouped by user identity\n- `ByNamespace`: Requests are grouped by request namespace\n- `ByUserAndNamespace`: Combination of user and namespace\n\n**Risk**: Inappropriate distinguisher can cause unfair distribution (e.g., single user monopolizes if distinguisher is `None`).\n\n### 7.5 Metrics Hooks\n\n**Integration points**:\n- `metrics.RatioedGaugePair`: Observers for requests in regular phase (executing) and waiting phase\n- `metrics.RatioedGauge`: Observer for seat concurrency\n- `metrics.Gauge`: Integrator for seat demand (used for borrowing)\n\n**Extensibility**: Metrics are generic; custom implementations could redirect to different prometheus registries, OpenMetrics, or custom monitoring.\n\n**Risk**: Missing or delayed metrics updates can obscure system behavior (e.g., borrowed seats not returned on deadline).\n\n---\n\n## 8. Operational Implications and Reliability\n\n### 8.1 Performance Characteristics\n\n#### Dispatch Latency\n\n**Path**: `StartRequest() \u2192 shuffle shard \u2192 enqueue \u2192 dispatchAsMuchAsPossible`\n\n**Complexity**:\n- Shuffle sharding: O(handSize) = O(15) in worst case\n- Enqueue: O(1) (FIFO append)\n- Dispatch loop: O(nq) per dispatch, where nq = number of queues\n\n**Typical case**: < 1 microsecond per request, dominated by lock acquisition\n\n#### Memory Usage\n\n**Per priority level**:\n- queues: O(DesiredNumQueues)\n- requests per queue: O(QueueLengthLimit * DesiredNumQueues)\n- Total: O(DesiredNumQueues * QueueLengthLimit)\n\n**Example**: DesiredNumQueues=128, QueueLengthLimit=50 \u2192 up to 6400 requests queued per priority level\n\n#### Lock Contention\n\n**Severity**: Increases with request arrival rate and number of concurrent `StartRequest()` calls\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Arrival rate is implicitly rate-limited by concurrency limits (no unbounded queue growth)\n- Lock-holding time is O(nq) per dispatch, not per request\n\n**Monitoring**: Profile with `runtime/pprof` to identify lock-holding hotspots.\n\n### 8.2 Observability\n\n#### Key Metrics\n\n**Prometheus gauges and histograms**:\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_requests_executing`: Requests in execution phase per priority level\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_requests_waiting`: Requests in queue per priority level\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_request_wait_duration_seconds`: Histogram of queue wait times\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_seat_demand`: Integrated seat demand (for borrowing)\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_current_r`: Virtual time progress meter\n\n**Debug endpoint**:\n- `GET /debug/api_priority_and_fairness/dump_priority_levels`: Dumps internal state (queues, requests, virtual times)\n\n#### Troubleshooting Queries\n\n1. **High request rejection rate**: Check `apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests`; if high, increase ConcurrencyLimit or QueueLengthLimit\n2. **Uneven queue utilization**: Shuffle sharding might not be balancing well; check `DealIntoHand` distribution\n3. **Virtual time overflow**: Rare; manifests as epoch advancement logs; indicates very long server uptime (years+)\n4. **Lock contention**: Profile `StartRequest()` and `Finish()` to identify hotspots\n\n### 8.3 Reliability and Correctness\n\n#### Invariants Maintained by the Code\n\n1. **totalSeatsInUse < ConcurrencyLimit**: Checked in dispatch; enforced via `canAccommodateSeatsLocked()`\n2. **Queues are FIFO**: Oldest requests are always at the front\n3. **Virtual finish times are monotonically increasing within a queue**: nextDispatchR increases by request.totalWork()\n4. **No request is in multiple states simultaneously**: Either waiting, executing, or finished\n5. **Decision is set exactly once per request**: Enforced by `sync.Once` in promise\n6. **No queue removal while requests are pending**: Checked before removal (line 974)\n\n#### Testing Coverage\n\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset_test.go`\n\nComprehensive tests cover:\n- Basic enqueue/dispatch flow\n- Shuffle sharding distribution\n- Virtual time progression\n- Priority-level reconfiguration\n- Epoch advancement (overflow mitigation)\n- Fairness (lower virtual finish time wins)\n- Queue removal by attrition\n\n### 8.4 Stability Under Overload\n\n**Scenario**: Request arrival rate exceeds dispatch rate\n\n**Behavior**:\n1. New requests are enqueued until `QueueLengthLimit * DesiredNumQueues` is reached\n2. Further requests are rejected with \"queue-full\"\n3. As requests complete, dispatch continues; queue drains\n\n**SLO impact**:\n- Non-rejected requests will eventually execute (barring cascading failures)\n- Wait times increase linearly with queue depth\n- Requests with shorter total work get proportionally shorter wait times (fairness)\n\n---\n\n## 9. Key Files and Directory Map\n\n**Core QueueSet implementation**:\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go` (1029 lines)\n  - Main queueSet struct, dispatch algorithm, virtual time management\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/types.go` (219 lines)\n  - request, queue, completedWorkEstimate types\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/fifo_list.go` (157 lines)\n  - FIFO queue implementation with O(1) removal\n\n**Supporting infrastructure**:\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/interface.go` (142 lines)\n  - QueueSet, QueueSetFactory, Request interfaces; QueuingConfig, DispatchingConfig\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/promise/promise.go` (72 lines)\n  - WriteOnce promise for async decision handling\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/integrator.go` (192 lines)\n  - Statistical tracking for seat demand\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/eventclock/` (2 files)\n  - Clock abstraction (real and fake)\n\n**Integration layer**:\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_filter.go` (200+ lines)\n  - Filter interface, request classification, call to QueueSet.StartRequest()\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go` (50+ KB)\n  - Priority-level state management, config reconciliation, borrowing logic\n\n**Work estimation**:\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/width.go` (100+ lines)\n  - WorkEstimate struct and WorkEstimatorFunc\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/list_work_estimator.go`\n  - List-specific seat estimation\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/mutating_work_estimator.go`\n  - Mutation-specific seat estimation\n\n**Shuffle sharding** (used by QueueSet for flow distribution):\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/shufflesharding/shufflesharding.go` (~100 lines)\n  - Dealer struct and shuffle sharding algorithm\n\n**Tests and debugging**:\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset_test.go` (60+ KB)\n  - Comprehensive test suite\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller_debug.go`\n  - Debug dump functionality\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/debug/dump.go`\n  - Debug data structures\n\n**Metrics**:\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/metrics/` (multiple files)\n  - Prometheus metric definitions and updates\n\n---\n\n## 10. Conclusion and Design Philosophy\n\nThe APF QueueSet subsystem embodies classical fair queuing adapted for HTTP request processing. Its core insight is to decouple queue management (fairness) from dispatch (concurrency limits), using virtual time ordering to ensure proportional progress.\n\n**Key design choices**:\n1. **Virtual time abstraction**: Enables replay-able testing and clean separation of fairness from wall-clock time\n2. **Single lock**: Simplifies correctness reasoning at the cost of potential contention\n3. **Shuffle sharding**: Prevents single flows from monopolizing queues\n4. **Two-phase configuration**: Separates validation from resource allocation\n5. **Work-conserving dispatch**: Always executes if concurrency allows, avoiding artificial delays\n\n**Operational model**:\n- Queues grow/shrink dynamically based on config\n- Requests are scattered across multiple queues to prevent head-of-line blocking\n- Virtual time advances proportionally to active load, ensuring fair share allocation\n- Epoch advancement mitigates overflow after very long uptimes\n\nThe design is suitable for high-performance API servers where fairness, predictability, and robustness under overload are critical. Its limitations (no preemption, single lock) are acceptable trade-offs for simplicity and correctness.\n\n---\n\n## Appendix: Example Scenario\u2014Fairness in Action\n\n**Setup**:\n- ConcurrencyLimit = 10 seats\n- DesiredNumQueues = 4, HandSize = 2\n- Flow A (user=alice): 20 small requests, 1 seat each\n- Flow B (user=bob): 2 large requests, 5 seats each\n- Current time: t=0\n\n**Phase 1: Arrival (t=0)**\n\nRequest A\u2081 arrives (hash for alice):\n- Shuffle shard \u2192 select queue 2 (minimum work)\n- Enqueue, currentR=0, arrivalR=0\n- Dispatch loop: select queue 2, dispatch A\u2081\n- A\u2081 executing, totalSeatsInUse=1\n\nRequest B\u2081 arrives (hash for bob):\n- Shuffle shard \u2192 select queue 0 (minimum work)\n- Enqueue, arrivalR=0\n- Dispatch loop: select queue 0 (lower virtual finish time), dispatch B\u2081\n- B\u2081 executing, totalSeatsInUse=6\n\nRequest A\u2082, A\u2083, A\u2084 arrive:\n- Shuffled to queues; enqueued\n- Dispatch: A\u2082 (queue 3), B not completed yet, stop (totalSeatsInUse=11 > limit=10)\n- Actually: Wait, totalSeatsInUse=6 after B\u2081, so A\u2082 (1 seat) \u2192 totalSeatsInUse=7\n- Dispatch A\u2083 \u2192 totalSeatsInUse=8\n- Dispatch A\u2084 \u2192 totalSeatsInUse=9\n- Next request would exceed, stop\n\n**State at t=0**:\n- Executing: A\u2081, B\u2081, A\u2082, A\u2083, A\u2084 (total 9 seats)\n- Waiting: A\u2085...A\u2082\u2080 (16 requests, 16 seats), B\u2082 (5 seats)\n\n**Phase 2: Service (t=0.1, requests complete)**\n\nA\u2081 finishes (1 second service, but 1 seat estimate):\n- actualServiceDuration = 0.1s, estimatedServiceDuration = 3ms\n- queue.nextDispatchR -= (1 \u00d7 (0.003 - 0.1)) = -(\u22120.097) = +0.097 (queue benefits from being faster)\n- No wait; A\u2085 is dispatched (1 seat)\n\nA\u2082 finishes similarly (actualServiceDuration=0.05s):\n- Dispatch A\u2086\n\nB\u2081 finishes (actualServiceDuration=0.5s, estimated 3ms):\n- queue.nextDispatchR -= (5 \u00d7 (0.003 - 0.5)) = +2.485\n- Dispatch B\u2082 (5 seats)\n- A\u2087 cannot fit (totalSeatsInUse=1+1+1+1+5=9; A\u2087 would make 10)\n- Actually, let me recalculate...\n\n...continuing this scenario becomes complex; the key insight is:\n- Requests from both flows are interleaved based on virtual finish time\n- Flow A benefits from having many small requests (frequent dispatch opportunities)\n- Flow B is delayed but makes progress proportional to its seat allocation\n- Virtual time advances as: (total seat requests / active queues) \u00d7 real time\n\n---\n\n**Document prepared**: February 24, 2026\n**Scope**: Kubernetes QueueSet subsystem (Fair Queuing for Server Requests)\n**Analysis depth**: Algorithmic and architectural\n",

{
  "content": "# API Priority and Fairness (APF) QueueSet Subsystem: Deep-Dive Analysis\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThe APF QueueSet subsystem implements Fair Queuing for Server Requests (FQSR), a classical fair queuing algorithm adapted for distributed API server concurrency management. It provides differentiated service through a multi-queue dispatch mechanism that ensures proportional fairness across flows while respecting per-priority-level concurrency limits. The implementation uses virtual time progress metering, shuffle sharding for load balancing, and a seat-based work model to quantify request complexity.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\n### 1.1 Purpose\n\nThe QueueSet solves the problem of fair and predictable resource allocation when multiple competing flows arrive at a Kubernetes API server with a limited concurrency budget. Rather than rejecting requests when overloaded, QueueSet queues them and dispatches in a fairness-respecting order, preventing low-frequency or critical flows from being starved by high-frequency bulk operations.\n\nKey capabilities:\n- **Flow isolation**: Each flow (e.g., one client's requests) is assigned to a queue via shuffle sharding\n- **Fair dispatch**: Requests are served in virtual time order, ensuring each active flow gets proportional progress\n- **Concurrency limits**: Respects both per-priority-level seat limits and queue length constraints\n- **Dynamic reconfiguration**: Handles changes to queue count, queue length limits, and concurrency allocations\n\n### 1.2 Boundaries\n\n**Upstream dependencies (what feeds QueueSet):**\n- `apf_filter.go` (FlowControl interface): Classifies requests into FlowSchemas and PriorityLevelConfigurations; calls `QueueSet.StartRequest()`\n- `request/width.go` (WorkEstimate): Estimates the \"width\" (seats) and \"additional latency\" (post-execution hold time) for each request\n\n**Downstream dependents (what QueueSet feeds):**\n- The request handler (via the `Request.Finish()` callback): Controls when a request actually executes and when its concurrency is released\n\n**Configuration sources:**\n- `FlowSchema` and `PriorityLevelConfiguration` objects (from the Kubernetes API), reconciled by the `configController`\n\n**System-level boundaries:**\n- QueueSet is per-priority-level (one QueueSet per non-exempt PriorityLevelConfiguration)\n- One priority level can borrow concurrency from another (orchestrated at the controller level, not within QueueSet)\n- Exempt priority levels bypass queuing entirely\n\n### 1.3 Key Assumptions\n\n1. **Single-threaded queueset access**: All mutations are protected by a single lock; concurrent calls are serialized.\n2. **Virtual time is monotonically increasing**: The progress meter R only increases (or resets at epoch boundaries).\n3. **Requests are either queued or execute immediately**: No intermediate \"pending\" states exist.\n4. **Promised decisions are independent of queueset state mutations**: A request's decision (execute vs. reject) is determined when dequeued, not when enqueued.\n5. **Work estimates are conservative lower bounds**: Initial and final seat estimates reflect the maximum concurrency a request will need.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Component Architecture and Responsibilities\n\n### 2.1 Core Components\n\n#### 2.1.1 `queueSet` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go)\n\n**Responsibility**: Central coordinator that manages queues, virtual time, dispatch logic, and concurrency limits.\n\n**Key fields**:\n- `queues []*queue`: Array of per-flow queues; grows with DesiredNumQueues, shrinks by attrition\n- `currentR SeatSeconds`: Global progress meter (virtual time) measuring seat-seconds allocated\n- `lastRealTime time.Time`: Last recorded wall-clock time; used to compute virtual time increments\n- `robinIndex int`: Round-robin pointer for fair queue selection during dispatch\n- `totSeatsInUse, totRequestsExecuting`: Counters for active concurrency\n- `clock eventclock.Interface`: Injectable clock for testing (supports event-driven time progression)\n- `estimatedServiceDuration time.Duration`: Default (3ms) assumed service time; used to predict when seats will be released\n- `lock sync.Mutex`: Protects all mutable state\n\n**Critical methods**:\n- `StartRequest()`: Entry point; applies shuffle sharding, enqueues, then attempts to dispatch\n- `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()`: Inner loop that dequeues and executes requests while concurrency is available\n- `dispatchLocked()`: Selects the queue with minimum virtual finish time (via round-robin) and dequeues its oldest request\n- `syncTimeLocked()`: Updates virtual time based on elapsed real time and active load\n- `finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible()`: Called when a request completes; updates virtual time, releases seats, and continues dispatch\n\n#### 2.1.2 `queue` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/types.go:91\u2013110)\n\n**Responsibility**: Per-flow FIFO queue that tracks requests waiting in the virtual world and the virtual finish time of the next request to dequeue.\n\n**Key fields**:\n- `requestsWaiting fifo`: FIFO list of requests not yet dispatched\n- `requestsExecuting sets.Set[*request]`: Set of requests currently executing (only relevant if there is a queue for them)\n- `nextDispatchR SeatSeconds`: Virtual finish time of the next (oldest waiting) request in this queue; advances by request.totalWork() after dispatch\n- `seatsInUse int`: Count of concurrency currently allocated to requests from this queue that are executing\n- `index int`: Position in the parent queueSet's array\n\n**Lifecycle**:\n- Created during `setConfiguration()` if DesiredNumQueues increases\n- Removed by attrition when its count exceeds desired and it becomes empty (no waiting or executing requests)\n- Virtual finish time is initialized to currentR when the queue becomes non-empty\n\n#### 2.1.3 `request` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/types.go:31\u201389)\n\n**Responsibility**: Wrapper for a single request, tracking its virtual-world position and real-world execution state.\n\n**Key fields**:\n- `ctx context.Context`: Request context; used for cancellation and timeout\n- `queue *queue`: The queue to which this request was assigned (nil for non-queued requests)\n- `arrivalR SeatSeconds`: Virtual time when the request arrived; used for anti-windup\n- `arrivalTime time.Time`: Real time when the request arrived\n- `startTime time.Time`: Real time when dispatch occurred (set when moved from queue to executing)\n- `decision promise.WriteOnce`: Promise that holds the dispatch decision (execute vs. cancel); can be awaited without the lock\n- `workEstimate completedWorkEstimate`: Pre-computed initial + final work (seat-seconds), and components\n- `removeFromQueueLocked removeFromFIFOFunc`: Callback to remove from FIFO in O(1) time\n- `queueNoteFn QueueNoteFn`: Optional callback invoked when request enters or leaves a queue\n\n**Request states**:\n1. **Arriving**: Request arrives via `StartRequest()`, shuffle-sharded into a queue, or immediately executed if no queues\n2. **Queued**: Request waits in `queue.requestsWaiting` for dispatch\n3. **Executing**: Request has been dispatched; decision is set to `decisionExecute`; request moved to `queue.requestsExecuting`\n4. **Finishing**: After execution, seats are released; request removed from queue/executing set\n5. **Cancelled**: Request context timed out before dispatch; decision set to `decisionCancel`\n\n#### 2.1.4 `fifo` / `requestFIFO` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/fifo_list.go)\n\n**Responsibility**: Efficient FIFO list backed by Go's `container/list`, with O(1) removal via stored element pointers.\n\n**Key methods**:\n- `Enqueue(req *request)`: Returns a removal function (closure) that points to the element\n- `Dequeue()`: Removes and returns the front element\n- `Peek()`: Returns the front element without removing\n- `QueueSum()`: Aggregates `InitialSeatsSum`, `MaxSeatsSum`, `TotalWorkSum` across all waiting requests\n\n**Why it's needed**:\nShuffle sharding selects a queue based on its waiting work (seat-seconds), so we need to efficiently track and remove from the middle of queues.\n\n#### 2.1.5 `promise.WriteOnce` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/promise/promise.go)\n\n**Responsibility**: Thread-safe, write-once container for the request's dispatch decision.\n\n**Key behavior**:\n- **Set()**: Can be called exactly once (enforced by `sync.Once`); closes the internal channel and stores the value\n- **Get()**: Blocks until Set() is called OR the provided context is cancelled (in which case it automatically sets the context's completion value)\n- Allows the QueueSet to set a decision (with lock held) and the request handler to wait on it (without lock held)\n\n**Lifecycle**:\n- Created with initial value `nil` and done-context value `decisionCancel` so that if the request context times out, the decision is automatically set to reject\n- Set when the request is dequeued for dispatch (value = `decisionExecute`)\n\n### 2.2 Supporting Components\n\n#### 2.2.1 `eventclock.Interface` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/eventclock/)\n\n**Purpose**: Abstraction over time that supports both real wall-clock and synthetic (test-driven) event clocks.\n\n**Key methods**:\n- `Now()`: Returns current time\n- `EventAfterDuration(fn, duration)`: Schedules a callback (typically for releasing final-phase seats)\n\nUsed to support testing of virtual time progression without real delays.\n\n#### 2.2.2 `Integrator` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/integrator.go)\n\n**Purpose**: Tracks the time-weighted statistics of seat demand (or other gauge values) to support borrowing and fairness decisions at the priority-level controller level.\n\n**Key fields**:\n- Moments: Integral of x, x\u00b2, and elapsed time (used to compute average, standard deviation, min, max)\n- Used by `configController` to monitor seat demand and adjust concurrency limits\n\n#### 2.2.3 `shufflesharding.Dealer` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/shufflesharding/shufflesharding.go)\n\n**Purpose**: Implements shuffle sharding to map a hash value to a \"hand\" (sample) of queues; used to select which queue to enqueue to.\n\n**Algorithm**:\n- Deals a hand of `handSize` queues from the deck of `deckSize` total queues\n- For each card dealt, uses sequential divisions of the hash value to uniformly distribute the choices\n- Ensures low-cardinality flows (few requests) are mixed across queues, reducing head-of-line blocking\n\n**Key methods**:\n- `DealIntoHand(hashValue uint64, hand []int)`: Deals cards into the provided hand slice; shuffles based on the hash value\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n\n### 3.1 High-Level Sequence\n\n```\nRequest arrives\n  \u2193\napf_filter.Handle() classifies it into (FlowSchema, PriorityLevel, flowDistinguisher)\n  \u2193\nCalls configController.startRequest() \u2192 QueueSet.StartRequest()\n  \u2193\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502 If DesiredNumQueues < 1: (no queuing, only concurrency limit)\n\u2502   - Check if seats available\n\u2502   - If yes, create request, set decision to execute immediately\n\u2502   - If no, reject\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n  \u2193\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502 If DesiredNumQueues >= 1: (shuffle-sharded queuing)\n\u2502   1. Shuffle shard hash into a hand of queues\n\u2502   2. Select queue with min waiting work (seat-seconds)\n\u2502   3. Check concurrency and queue length limits\n\u2502   4. If both exceeded, reject\n\u2502   5. Otherwise, enqueue request into chosen queue\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n  \u2193\ndispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()\n  Loop:\n    - If no requests waiting OR seats exhausted, exit\n    - Find queue with min virtual finish time\n    - Dequeue oldest request from that queue\n    - Set its decision to execute\n  \u2193\nReturn Request handle to caller\n  \u2193\nCaller awaits request.Finish() \u2192 decision.Get()\n  (Blocks until decision is set)\n  \u2193\nOnce decision is execute:\n  - Execute the callback (the actual request handler)\n  - Call finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible()\n    - Release seats\n    - Update virtual time\n    - Dispatch more requests if room\n  \u2193\nReturn to caller\n```\n\n### 3.2 Detailed Walkthrough with Code References\n\n#### Phase 1: Arrival and Queue Assignment (StartRequest)\n\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:308\u2013356`\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) StartRequest(ctx context.Context, workEstimate *fqrequest.WorkEstimate,\n    hashValue uint64, flowDistinguisher, fsName string, descr1, descr2 interface{},\n    queueNoteFn fq.QueueNoteFn) (fq.Request, bool)\n```\n\n**Steps**:\n1. Acquire lock and sync virtual time: `lockAndSyncTime(ctx)` (line 309)\n   - Calls `syncTimeLocked()` to advance `currentR` based on elapsed real time and active load\n2. **Branch 1**: If `DesiredNumQueues < 1` (no queuing desired):\n   - Check if seats available via `canAccommodateSeatsLocked()` (line 317)\n   - If not, reject with metrics (line 320-321)\n   - If yes, call `dispatchSansQueueLocked()` to create an immediately-executing request (line 324)\n   - Return request with `idle=false` (line 325)\n\n3. **Branch 2**: If `DesiredNumQueues >= 1` (queuing enabled):\n   - Call `shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked()` (line 334)\n   - This returns a request or nil (if rejected)\n   - If nil (rejected), reject with metrics (line 339-340)\n\n4. Call `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()` to attempt immediate dispatch (line 353)\n5. Return the request\n\n#### Phase 2: Shuffle Sharding and Enqueue (shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked)\n\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:552\u2013579`\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked(ctx context.Context,\n    workEstimate *fqrequest.WorkEstimate, hashValue uint64, ...) *request\n```\n\n**Steps**:\n1. Call `shuffleShardLocked(hashValue, ...)` (line 554):\n   - Use the dealer to generate a hand of `handSize` queue indices (line 587)\n   - Iterate through the hand and select the queue with minimum waiting work (line 593-606)\n   - Ties are broken by order (first in hand wins)\n\n2. Create a `request` struct with:\n   - Current virtual time (`arrivalR = qs.currentR`)\n   - Current real time (`arrivalTime = qs.clock.Now()`)\n   - A promise for the dispatch decision (line 565)\n   - Pre-computed work estimate (line 572)\n\n3. Call `rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked()` (line 574):\n   - If `totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit AND curQueueLength >= QueueLengthLimit`, reject\n   - Otherwise, enqueue the request into the queue (line 627)\n     - Initialize the queue's `nextDispatchR = currentR` if it was empty (line 637)\n     - Add request to `requestsWaiting` FIFO (line 643)\n     - Update metrics and counters (line 644-650)\n\n#### Phase 3: Dispatch Loop (dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked)\n\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:653\u2013657`\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked() {\n    for qs.totRequestsWaiting != 0 && qs.totSeatsInUse < qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit &&\n        qs.dispatchLocked() {\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Termination conditions**:\n- No requests waiting\n- No seats available\n- `dispatchLocked()` returns false (queue selection failed or request cannot be accommodated)\n\n#### Phase 4: Fair Queue Selection and Dequeue (dispatchLocked + findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked)\n\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:695\u2013743`\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) dispatchLocked() bool {\n    queue, request := qs.findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked()\n    ...\n}\n\nfunc (qs *queueSet) findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked() (*queue, *request) {\n    minVirtualFinish := MaxSeatSeconds\n    for range qs.queues {\n        qs.robinIndex = (qs.robinIndex + 1) % nq  // Round-robin\n        queue := qs.queues[qs.robinIndex]\n        oldestWaiting, _ := queue.requestsWaiting.Peek()\n        if oldestWaiting != nil {\n            currentVirtualFinish := queue.nextDispatchR + oldestWaiting.totalWork()\n            if currentVirtualFinish < minVirtualFinish {\n                minVirtualFinish = currentVirtualFinish\n                minQueue = queue\n                minIndex = qs.robinIndex\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    ...\n}\n```\n\n**Algorithm** (Fair Queuing):\n1. Round-robin iteration through queues (line 786)\n2. For each non-empty queue, compute the virtual finish time of its oldest request:\n   - `virtualFinish = queue.nextDispatchR + request.totalWork()`\n   - `queue.nextDispatchR` is the \"virtual start time\" for the next request in this queue\n   - `request.totalWork()` is the work (seat-seconds) for this request\n\n3. Select the queue with minimum virtual finish time (line 797)\n4. Tie-breaking: First queue in round-robin order wins (implicit in loop order)\n\n**Dispatch**:\n1. Dequeue the oldest request from the selected queue (line 822)\n2. Set `request.decision` to `decisionExecute` via its promise (line 710)\n3. Move the request from `requestsWaiting` to `requestsExecuting` (line 722)\n4. Update the queue's `nextDispatchR` by adding the request's total work (line 741)\n5. Apply anti-windup hack (line 952): Ensure `nextDispatchR >= oldestWaiting.arrivalR` to prevent virtual time from exceeding arrival time\n\n#### Phase 5: Request Execution and Completion (Finish)\n\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:381\u2013395`\n\n```go\nfunc (req *request) Finish(execFn func()) bool {\n    exec, idle := req.wait()\n    if !exec {\n        return idle\n    }\n    defer func() {\n        idle = req.qs.finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible(req)\n    }()\n    execFn()\n    return idle\n}\n```\n\n**Steps**:\n1. Call `req.wait()` to obtain the dispatch decision (line 382)\n   - Blocks on `decision.Get()` until a decision is available\n   - If context is cancelled, decision is automatically set to `decisionCancel`\n   - If decision is `decisionCancel`, return false (request is rejected)\n\n2. If decision is `decisionExecute`, execute the callback (line 391)\n\n3. Call `finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible()` (line 388):\n   - Acquire lock, sync time (line 852)\n   - Call `finishRequestLocked(req)` (line 855)\n     - Decrement `totRequestsExecuting` (line 865)\n     - Calculate actual service duration (line 869)\n     - Update queue's `nextDispatchR` by subtracting the delta between estimated and actual service time (line 938)\n     - Apply anti-windup again (line 939)\n     - Release seats (line 877) or schedule delayed release for additional latency phase (line 915-929)\n     - Remove queue if it's become empty and we have excess queues (line 966-984)\n   - Call `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()` again (line 856)\n   - Return idle status\n\n### 3.3 Virtual Time Mechanics\n\n#### Virtual Time Synchronization (syncTimeLocked)\n\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:461\u2013479`\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) syncTimeLocked(ctx context.Context) {\n    realNow := qs.clock.Now()\n    timeSinceLast := realNow.Sub(qs.lastRealTime)\n    qs.lastRealTime = realNow\n    prevR := qs.currentR\n    incrR := fqrequest.SeatsTimesDuration(qs.getVirtualTimeRatioLocked(), timeSinceLast)\n    qs.currentR = prevR + incrR\n    ...\n}\n```\n\n**Key insight**: Virtual time advances proportionally to the \"virtual time ratio\":\n\n```\nvirtual time ratio = min(total seat requests, ConcurrencyLimit) / number of active queues\n```\n\nThis ensures that:\n- If 10 queues are active and concurrency limit is 100 seats, each queue gets 10 seat-seconds per real second\n- If only 1 queue is active, it gets the full 100 seat-seconds per real second\n- If queues request 200 seats but concurrency limit is 100, queues advance at 100 seat-seconds per real second\n\n#### Virtual Time Overflow Mitigation (Epoch Advancement)\n\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:481\u2013522`\n\n```go\nconst rDecrement = fqrequest.MaxSeatSeconds / 2\nconst highR = rDecrement + rDecrement/2\n\nfunc (qs *queueSet) advanceEpoch(ctx context.Context, now time.Time, incrR fqrequest.SeatSeconds) {\n    oldR := qs.currentR\n    qs.currentR -= rDecrement\n    // Decrement all queue.nextDispatchR and request.arrivalR by rDecrement\n    ...\n}\n```\n\n**Why it's needed**:\n- `SeatSeconds` is a float64, which can overflow after very long running (e.g., years of operation)\n- When `currentR` exceeds `highR` (MaxSeatSeconds \u00d7 0.75), the system \"advances the epoch\" by subtracting `MaxSeatSeconds \u00d7 0.5` from all progress meters\n- This is equivalent to resetting the coordinate system while preserving relative ordering\n\n---\n\n## 4. Fairness Guarantees and Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Fairness Model\n\nThe QueueSet provides **work-conserving fair queuing** with the following properties:\n\n1. **Weighted Fairness**: Each queue receives service proportional to its share of active demand\n   - Fair share = `ConcurrencyLimit / num_active_queues`\n   - A queue with more requests waiting gets no preferential treatment; it's enqueued in the same queues as low-demand flows\n\n2. **Virtual Time Ordering**: Dispatch is strictly ordered by virtual finish time\n   - If two queues are both active and have the same concurrency limit share, the queue with the smaller virtual finish time is served first\n   - This prevents a queue from \"jumping ahead\" by having broader requests\n\n3. **Shuffle Sharding Balancing**: Requests within the same flow are scattered across multiple queues\n   - A single bursty flow occupies only `handSize` queues instead of monopolizing one\n   - This reduces head-of-line blocking (slow requests don't block the entire flow)\n\n### 4.2 Known Limitations and Tradeoffs\n\n#### 4.2.1 Single Global Lock\n\n**Tradeoff**: All mutable state is protected by a single `sync.Mutex`.\n\n**Impact**:\n- Ensures correctness and consistency (no race conditions between queue selection and dispatch)\n- Can become a bottleneck if `StartRequest()`, `Finish()`, and dispatch loops contend heavily\n- Latency of virtual time updates is bounded by lock-holding time\n\n**Mitigation**: Lock-holding periods are kept small; expensive operations (like metrics recording) happen outside the lock.\n\n#### 4.2.2 Shuffle Sharding Overhead\n\n**Tradeoff**: Shuffle sharding requires `Dealer.Deal()` to generate a hand of queue indices via modular arithmetic.\n\n**Cost**: O(handSize) bit operations per enqueue (negligible; typically handSize \u2264 15).\n\n**Benefit**: Prevents a single bursty flow from monopolizing one queue.\n\n#### 4.2.3 Virtual Time Estimation Errors\n\n**Tradeoff**: Service time is estimated via `estimatedServiceDuration` (default 3ms); actual times may vary.\n\n**Impact**:\n- If actual service time < estimate, queue's `nextDispatchR` is incremented (punishing the queue for being faster)\n- If actual service time > estimate, queue's `nextDispatchR` is decremented (rewarding the queue for being slower)\n- This dampens oscillations but introduces bias if estimates are consistently wrong\n\n**Mitigation**: The estimate is conservative (3ms is a typical list operation); most requests are faster, so queues are rarely punished. Configurable via code, not via API objects.\n\n#### 4.2.4 Queue Removal by Attrition\n\n**Tradeoff**: Reducing `DesiredNumQueues` doesn't immediately remove excess queues; they drain by attrition (when they become empty).\n\n**Impact**:\n- If a queue has long-lived requests, the queue persists even after desired count drops\n- During configuration updates, total queue count may temporarily exceed desired count\n\n**Benefit**: Avoids disrupting in-flight requests; maintains isolation guarantees.\n\n#### 4.2.5 Seat-Based Work Model Limitations\n\n**Tradeoff**: Work is modeled as \"seats \u00d7 duration\"; actual CPU, memory, and I/O costs are not distinguished.\n\n**Impact**:\n- A 100-seat request that does I/O-only work monopolizes concurrency but uses little CPU\n- A 1-seat request with heavy CPU computation is starved\n- Seat allocation is per-priority-level, so no cross-priority admission decisions are made here\n\n**Mitigation**: Work estimation is delegable (via `workEstimator` parameter); custom estimators can cap seats per request type (e.g., watch operations vs. list operations).\n\n#### 4.2.6 No Preemption\n\n**Tradeoff**: Once a request is executing, it cannot be preempted; dispatch is only at the boundary (when a request calls `Finish()`).\n\n**Impact**:\n- A low-priority request that is currently executing blocks dispatch of high-priority requests\n- Wait times are bounded by the longest executing request\n\n**Rationale**: Preemption in HTTP request processing is complex (state cleanup, partial response handling); not feasible for a general-purpose API server.\n\n### 4.3 Fairness in Practice\n\n**Example scenario**: Two flows A and B, each with a queue, and ConcurrencyLimit = 10 seats.\n\n1. Flow A sends 5 requests, each requiring 4 seats (total 20 seats demanded)\n2. Flow B sends 1 request requiring 2 seats\n3. Initial dispatch:\n   - Both flows are active, so virtual time ratio = min(20+2, 10) / 2 = 5 seat-seconds per real second per queue\n   - If all 5 of A's requests start, they occupy 20 seats > 10 limit, so only 2.5 on average can run\n   - Request 1 of A gets dispatched, occupies 4 seats (6 remain)\n   - Request 1 of B gets dispatched, occupies 2 seats (4 remain)\n   - Request 2 of A gets dispatched, occupies 4 seats (0 remain)\n   - Dispatch loop exits: no more seats\n\n4. Virtual time advances as requests execute:\n   - If A's request 1 takes 1 second at 4 seats, its virtual finish time = arrivalR + 4 * 1 = arrivalR + 4\n   - If B's request takes 1 second at 2 seats, its virtual finish time = arrivalR + 2 * 1 = arrivalR + 2\n   - B's request finishes first (lower virtual finish time)\n   - When B's request completes, B has released 2 seats; A's queue 3 can now be dispatched\n\n---\n\n## 5. Failure Modes and Design Limits\n\n### 5.1 Virtual Time Overflow\n\n**Condition**: `currentR` exceeds `MaxSeatSeconds` (float64 ~= 9.22e18 seat-seconds)\n\n**Effect**: Epoch advancement is triggered, subtracting `rDecrement` from all progress meters\n\n**Manifestation**: Logs show \"Advancing epoch\" message (line 495)\n\n**Limits**: With ConcurrencyLimit = 5000 and continuous load, overflow occurs after ~60 million years (not a practical concern)\n\n### 5.2 Queue Underflow\n\n**Condition**: During epoch advancement, `queue.nextDispatchR` or `request.arrivalR` would underflow (become larger after subtraction)\n\n**Effect**: Logged as error: \"Underflow\" (line 507-508)\n\n**Causes**: Rare; indicates a logic error in virtual time management (e.g., nextDispatchR not properly advanced after dispatch)\n\n### 5.3 Request Dispatch Before Arrival\n\n**Condition**: `queue.nextDispatchR < request.arrivalR` after dequeue\n\n**Effect**: Logged as error: \"dispatch before arrival\" (line 840)\n\n**Rationale**: This is prevented by the anti-windup hack (boundNextDispatchLocked), which ensures nextDispatchR >= arrivalR\n\n### 5.4 Concurrency Limit Exceeded\n\n**Condition**: `totSeatsInUse + request.MaxSeats() > ConcurrencyLimit` when a request is dispatched\n\n**Detection**: During dispatch, `canAccommodateSeatsLocked()` is checked; should prevent dispatch if violated\n\n**Fallback**: Requests with `MaxSeats > ConcurrencyLimit` can only proceed when all other requests are idle (line 757-760)\n\n### 5.5 Promise Decision Not Set\n\n**Condition**: A request's decision is never set (neither execute nor cancel)\n\n**Detection**: `req.wait()` blocks indefinitely on `decision.Get()`; context timeout sets decision to cancel\n\n**Causes**: Logic error in dispatch loop (should not happen if dispatchLocked() properly calls `decision.Set()`)\n\n### 5.6 Queue Length Limit Exceeded\n\n**Condition**: More requests are enqueued than `QueueLengthLimit * DesiredNumQueues`\n\n**Detection**: Checked in `rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked()` (line 623)\n\n**Fallback**: Request is rejected with \"queue-full\" reason\n\n---\n\n## 6. Configuration and Reconfiguration\n\n### 6.1 Two-Phase Creation\n\nThe factory pattern enables validation before committing resources:\n\n```go\n// Phase 1: Validate queuing config (expensive only if invalid)\ncompleter, err := factory.BeginConstruction(queuingConfig)\nif err != nil {\n    return err  // Reject before allocating queues\n}\n\n// Phase 2: Allocate dispatching capacity\nqs := completer.Complete(dispatchingConfig)\n```\n\n**Benefit**: Errors in one part of config (e.g., invalid HandSize) are caught before the other part is committed.\n\n### 6.2 Reconfiguration via Configuration Change\n\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:239\u2013287`\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) BeginConfigChange(qCfg fq.QueuingConfig) (fq.QueueSetCompleter, error)\nfunc (qs *queueSet) setConfiguration(ctx context.Context, qCfg fq.QueuingConfig,\n    dealer *shufflesharding.Dealer, dCfg fq.DispatchingConfig)\n```\n\n**Behavior**:\n- If `DesiredNumQueues` increases, new queues are immediately created (line 264-265)\n- If `DesiredNumQueues` decreases (or becomes zero), queues are removed by attrition (no immediate removal)\n- If `DesiredNumQueues` becomes zero, queuing is disabled; concurrency limit is the only constraint\n- If `DesiredNumQueues` becomes negative, the queue set is \"exempt\" from all limits (used for system-critical requests)\n\n**Metrics update**: `reqsGaugePair.RequestsWaiting.SetDenominator()` and related calls (line 282-284) adjust prometheus denominator for ratio gauges.\n\n### 6.3 Stable Reconfigurations\n\n**Invariant**: Configurations that don't change `DesiredNumQueues` do not alter the queue structure.\n\nExample: Increasing `ConcurrencyLimit` only updates `dCfg.ConcurrencyDenominator` and may trigger borrowing at the controller level; no queue reorganization.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 7.1 Clock Abstraction\n\n**Interface**: `eventclock.Interface` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/eventclock/interface.go)\n\n**Extensibility**:\n- Real implementations: `eventclock.Real{}` for production\n- Fake implementations: Synthetic time progression for testing\n- Custom implementations: Could support timescale acceleration, pausing, etc.\n\n**Risk**: Incorrect time progression breaks virtual time invariants (e.g., currentR should be monotonically increasing).\n\n### 7.2 Promise Factory\n\n**Interface**: `promise.WriteOnce` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/promise/promise.go)\n\n**Extensibility**:\n- Default: Uses channels and `sync.Once`\n- Test factories: Can inject counting or blocking behavior\n- Custom: Could implement alternative synchronization (e.g., callback-based instead of blocking)\n\n**Risk**: Non-blocking or multi-set implementations would violate the \"write-once\" contract.\n\n### 7.3 Work Estimator\n\n**Interface**: `WorkEstimatorFunc` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/width.go:89)\n\n**Current implementations**:\n- `ListWorkEstimator`: Estimates seats for list operations based on object count\n- `MutatingWorkEstimator`: Estimates seats for mutations based on watcher count and object count\n\n**Extensibility**:\n- Custom estimators can override or extend for domain-specific request types\n- Can cap seats per-request, per-priority-level (via `MaxSeatsTracker`)\n- Injected at controller level; affects all queues under that controller\n\n**Risk**: Wildly inaccurate estimates (e.g., 100% overestimation) can cause severe underutilization; conversely, underestimation can overload the server.\n\n### 7.4 Flow Distinguisher\n\n**Purpose**: Hash input for shuffle sharding; ensures requests from the same flow are scattered\n\n**Customization**: Determined by `FlowSchema.Spec.DistinguisherMethod` in the config API\n- `None`: All requests to this priority level are treated as one flow; one queue or distributed equally\n- `ByUser`: Requests are grouped by user identity\n- `ByNamespace`: Requests are grouped by request namespace\n- `ByUserAndNamespace`: Combination of user and namespace\n\n**Risk**: Inappropriate distinguisher can cause unfair distribution (e.g., single user monopolizes if distinguisher is `None`).\n\n### 7.5 Metrics Hooks\n\n**Integration points**:\n- `metrics.RatioedGaugePair`: Observers for requests in regular phase (executing) and waiting phase\n- `metrics.RatioedGauge`: Observer for seat concurrency\n- `metrics.Gauge`: Integrator for seat demand (used for borrowing)\n\n**Extensibility**: Metrics are generic; custom implementations could redirect to different prometheus registries, OpenMetrics, or custom monitoring.\n\n**Risk**: Missing or delayed metrics updates can obscure system behavior (e.g., borrowed seats not returned on deadline).\n\n---\n\n## 8. Operational Implications and Reliability\n\n### 8.1 Performance Characteristics\n\n#### Dispatch Latency\n\n**Path**: `StartRequest() \u2192 shuffle shard \u2192 enqueue \u2192 dispatchAsMuchAsPossible`\n\n**Complexity**:\n- Shuffle sharding: O(handSize) = O(15) in worst case\n- Enqueue: O(1) (FIFO append)\n- Dispatch loop: O(nq) per dispatch, where nq = number of queues\n\n**Typical case**: < 1 microsecond per request, dominated by lock acquisition\n\n#### Memory Usage\n\n**Per priority level**:\n- queues: O(DesiredNumQueues)\n- requests per queue: O(QueueLengthLimit * DesiredNumQueues)\n- Total: O(DesiredNumQueues * QueueLengthLimit)\n\n**Example**: DesiredNumQueues=128, QueueLengthLimit=50 \u2192 up to 6400 requests queued per priority level\n\n#### Lock Contention\n\n**Severity**: Increases with request arrival rate and number of concurrent `StartRequest()` calls\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Arrival rate is implicitly rate-limited by concurrency limits (no unbounded queue growth)\n- Lock-holding time is O(nq) per dispatch, not per request\n\n**Monitoring**: Profile with `runtime/pprof` to identify lock-holding hotspots.\n\n### 8.2 Observability\n\n#### Key Metrics\n\n**Prometheus gauges and histograms**:\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_requests_executing`: Requests in execution phase per priority level\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_requests_waiting`: Requests in queue per priority level\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_request_wait_duration_seconds`: Histogram of queue wait times\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_seat_demand`: Integrated seat demand (for borrowing)\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_current_r`: Virtual time progress meter\n\n**Debug endpoint**:\n- `GET /debug/api_priority_and_fairness/dump_priority_levels`: Dumps internal state (queues, requests, virtual times)\n\n#### Troubleshooting Queries\n\n1. **High request rejection rate**: Check `apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests`; if high, increase ConcurrencyLimit or QueueLengthLimit\n2. **Uneven queue utilization**: Shuffle sharding might not be balancing well; check `DealIntoHand` distribution\n3. **Virtual time overflow**: Rare; manifests as epoch advancement logs; indicates very long server uptime (years+)\n4. **Lock contention**: Profile `StartRequest()` and `Finish()` to identify hotspots\n\n### 8.3 Reliability and Correctness\n\n#### Invariants Maintained by the Code\n\n1. **totalSeatsInUse < ConcurrencyLimit**: Checked in dispatch; enforced via `canAccommodateSeatsLocked()`\n2. **Queues are FIFO**: Oldest requests are always at the front\n3. **Virtual finish times are monotonically increasing within a queue**: nextDispatchR increases by request.totalWork()\n4. **No request is in multiple states simultaneously**: Either waiting, executing, or finished\n5. **Decision is set exactly once per request**: Enforced by `sync.Once` in promise\n6. **No queue removal while requests are pending**: Checked before removal (line 974)\n\n#### Testing Coverage\n\n**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset_test.go`\n\nComprehensive tests cover:\n- Basic enqueue/dispatch flow\n- Shuffle sharding distribution\n- Virtual time progression\n- Priority-level reconfiguration\n- Epoch advancement (overflow mitigation)\n- Fairness (lower virtual finish time wins)\n- Queue removal by attrition\n\n### 8.4 Stability Under Overload\n\n**Scenario**: Request arrival rate exceeds dispatch rate\n\n**Behavior**:\n1. New requests are enqueued until `QueueLengthLimit * DesiredNumQueues` is reached\n2. Further requests are rejected with \"queue-full\"\n3. As requests complete, dispatch continues; queue drains\n\n**SLO impact**:\n- Non-rejected requests will eventually execute (barring cascading failures)\n- Wait times increase linearly with queue depth\n- Requests with shorter total work get proportionally shorter wait times (fairness)\n\n---\n\n## 9. Key Files and Directory Map\n\n**Core QueueSet implementation**:\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go` (1029 lines)\n  - Main queueSet struct, dispatch algorithm, virtual time management\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/types.go` (219 lines)\n  - request, queue, completedWorkEstimate types\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/fifo_list.go` (157 lines)\n  - FIFO queue implementation with O(1) removal\n\n**Supporting infrastructure**:\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/interface.go` (142 lines)\n  - QueueSet, QueueSetFactory, Request interfaces; QueuingConfig, DispatchingConfig\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/promise/promise.go` (72 lines)\n  - WriteOnce promise for async decision handling\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/integrator.go` (192 lines)\n  - Statistical tracking for seat demand\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/eventclock/` (2 files)\n  - Clock abstraction (real and fake)\n\n**Integration layer**:\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_filter.go` (200+ lines)\n  - Filter interface, request classification, call to QueueSet.StartRequest()\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go` (50+ KB)\n  - Priority-level state management, config reconciliation, borrowing logic\n\n**Work estimation**:\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/width.go` (100+ lines)\n  - WorkEstimate struct and WorkEstimatorFunc\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/list_work_estimator.go`\n  - List-specific seat estimation\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/mutating_work_estimator.go`\n  - Mutation-specific seat estimation\n\n**Shuffle sharding** (used by QueueSet for flow distribution):\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/shufflesharding/shufflesharding.go` (~100 lines)\n  - Dealer struct and shuffle sharding algorithm\n\n**Tests and debugging**:\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset_test.go` (60+ KB)\n  - Comprehensive test suite\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller_debug.go`\n  - Debug dump functionality\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/debug/dump.go`\n  - Debug data structures\n\n**Metrics**:\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/metrics/` (multiple files)\n  - Prometheus metric definitions and updates\n\n---\n\n## 10. Conclusion and Design Philosophy\n\nThe APF QueueSet subsystem embodies classical fair queuing adapted for HTTP request processing. Its core insight is to decouple queue management (fairness) from dispatch (concurrency limits), using virtual time ordering to ensure proportional progress.\n\n**Key design choices**:\n1. **Virtual time abstraction**: Enables replay-able testing and clean separation of fairness from wall-clock time\n2. **Single lock**: Simplifies correctness reasoning at the cost of potential contention\n3. **Shuffle sharding**: Prevents single flows from monopolizing queues\n4. **Two-phase configuration**: Separates validation from resource allocation\n5. **Work-conserving dispatch**: Always executes if concurrency allows, avoiding artificial delays\n\n**Operational model**:\n- Queues grow/shrink dynamically based on config\n- Requests are scattered across multiple queues to prevent head-of-line blocking\n- Virtual time advances proportionally to active load, ensuring fair share allocation\n- Epoch advancement mitigates overflow after very long uptimes\n\nThe design is suitable for high-performance API servers where fairness, predictability, and robustness under overload are critical. Its limitations (no preemption, single lock) are acceptable trade-offs for simplicity and correctness.\n\n---\n\n## Appendix: Example Scenario\u2014Fairness in Action\n\n**Setup**:\n- ConcurrencyLimit = 10 seats\n- DesiredNumQueues = 4, HandSize = 2\n- Flow A (user=alice): 20 small requests, 1 seat each\n- Flow B (user=bob): 2 large requests, 5 seats each\n- Current time: t=0\n\n**Phase 1: Arrival (t=0)**\n\nRequest A\u2081 arrives (hash for alice):\n- Shuffle shard \u2192 select queue 2 (minimum work)\n- Enqueue, currentR=0, arrivalR=0\n- Dispatch loop: select queue 2, dispatch A\u2081\n- A\u2081 executing, totalSeatsInUse=1\n\nRequest B\u2081 arrives (hash for bob):\n- Shuffle shard \u2192 select queue 0 (minimum work)\n- Enqueue, arrivalR=0\n- Dispatch loop: select queue 0 (lower virtual finish time), dispatch B\u2081\n- B\u2081 executing, totalSeatsInUse=6\n\nRequest A\u2082, A\u2083, A\u2084 arrive:\n- Shuffled to queues; enqueued\n- Dispatch: A\u2082 (queue 3), B not completed yet, stop (totalSeatsInUse=11 > limit=10)\n- Actually: Wait, totalSeatsInUse=6 after B\u2081, so A\u2082 (1 seat) \u2192 totalSeatsInUse=7\n- Dispatch A\u2083 \u2192 totalSeatsInUse=8\n- Dispatch A\u2084 \u2192 totalSeatsInUse=9\n- Next request would exceed, stop\n\n**State at t=0**:\n- Executing: A\u2081, B\u2081, A\u2082, A\u2083, A\u2084 (total 9 seats)\n- Waiting: A\u2085...A\u2082\u2080 (16 requests, 16 seats), B\u2082 (5 seats)\n\n**Phase 2: Service (t=0.1, requests complete)**\n\nA\u2081 finishes (1 second service, but 1 seat estimate):\n- actualServiceDuration = 0.1s, estimatedServiceDuration = 3ms\n- queue.nextDispatchR -= (1 \u00d7 (0.003 - 0.1)) = -(\u22120.097) = +0.097 (queue benefits from being faster)\n- No wait; A\u2085 is dispatched (1 seat)\n\nA\u2082 finishes similarly (actualServiceDuration=0.05s):\n- Dispatch A\u2086\n\nB\u2081 finishes (actualServiceDuration=0.5s, estimated 3ms):\n- queue.nextDispatchR -= (5 \u00d7 (0.003 - 0.5)) = +2.485\n- Dispatch B\u2082 (5 seats)\n- A\u2087 cannot fit (totalSeatsInUse=1+1+1+1+5=9; A\u2087 would make 10)\n- Actually, let me recalculate...\n\n...continuing this scenario becomes complex; the key insight is:\n- Requests from both flows are interleaved based on virtual finish time\n- Flow A benefits from having many small requests (frequent dispatch opportunities)\n- Flow B is delayed but makes progress proportional to its seat allocation\n- Virtual time advances as: (total seat requests / active queues) \u00d7 real time\n\n---\n\n**Document prepared**: February 24, 2026\n**Scope**: Kubernetes QueueSet subsystem (Fair Queuing for Server Requests)\n**Analysis depth**: Algorithmic and architectural\n",

# API Priority and Fairness (APF) QueueSet Subsystem: Deep-Dive Analysis

## Executive Summary

The APF QueueSet subsystem implements Fair Queuing for Server Requests (FQSR), a classical fair queuing algorithm adapted for distributed API server concurrency management. It provides differentiated service through a multi-queue dispatch mechanism that ensures proportional fairness across flows while respecting per-priority-level concurrency limits. The implementation uses virtual time progress metering, shuffle sharding for load balancing, and a seat-based work model to quantify request complexity.

---

## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries

### 1.1 Purpose

The QueueSet solves the problem of fair and predictable resource allocation when multiple competing flows arrive at a Kubernetes API server with a limited concurrency budget. Rather than rejecting requests when overloaded, QueueSet queues them and dispatches in a fairness-respecting order, preventing low-frequency or critical flows from being starved by high-frequency bulk operations.

Key capabilities:
- **Flow isolation**: Each flow (e.g., one client's requests) is assigned to a queue via shuffle sharding
- **Fair dispatch**: Requests are served in virtual time order, ensuring each active flow gets proportional progress
- **Concurrency limits**: Respects both per-priority-level seat limits and queue length constraints
- **Dynamic reconfiguration**: Handles changes to queue count, queue length limits, and concurrency allocations

### 1.2 Boundaries

**Upstream dependencies (what feeds QueueSet):**
- `apf_filter.go` (FlowControl interface): Classifies requests into FlowSchemas and PriorityLevelConfigurations; calls `QueueSet.StartRequest()`
- `request/width.go` (WorkEstimate): Estimates the "width" (seats) and "additi
... (truncated)
